B008A1TIOK|5.0|Whether out of pure curiosity or out of admiration for the Vivaldi's Four Seasons or because of admiration for Daniel Hope's violin virtuosity - or even perhaps an admirer of Max Richter, this new creation is something that is a `must hear', `must own.'  This is one of the most pleasant surprises of the year - a second look at the famous Vivaldi work that we all know and love. The primary genius behind this venture is new-music maestro Max Richter, a German born British composer who studied composition and piano at University of Edinburgh, the Royal Academy of Music and with Luciano Berio in Florence. After finishing his studies, Richter co-founded the contemporary classical ensemble Piano Circus. He stayed with the group for ten years, commissioning and performing works by Arvo P&auml;rt, Brian Eno, Philip Glass, Julia Wolfe and Steve Reich. And now Richter turns to the past and brings us the well-known Four Seasons with a spring-cleaning.<br /><br />Adding a `prelude' to the original beginning of the work, Richter lets the mood of a shimmering, almost popping out of the bud Spring by juxtaposing electronic and acoustic strings and then gradually after 42 seconds the opening of Vivaldi's work begins.  Daniel Hope is the gifted performer here with the Konzerthaus Kammerorchester Berlin conducted by Andre de Ridder. What happens as we progress through spring and summer and autumn to winter is a sifting through the extraneous portions of these works to simplify and make the solo violin lines more elegant and atmospheric. No, it does not come across as a `Stokowski rethinks Bach' extravaganza - quite the opposite.  This is crystalline pure Vivaldi polished to a fair-thee-well by Richter. According to Richter, `\\"The Four Seasons is something we all carry around with us. It's just everywhere. In a way, we stop being able to hear it. So this project is about reclaiming this music for me personally, by getting inside it and rediscovering it for myself - and taking a new path through a well-known landscape.' The result is full of charm, exquisitely played, and makes the entire sequence of seasons comes refreshingly alive. Grady Harp, November 12hrough a well-known landscape.' However, some of those same critical observations can also be directed at \\"2001: A Space Odyssey\\", \\"Star Wars\\", or even 1979's \\"Alien\\", all considered by most to be worthwhile movies, if not sci-fi classics. And much of what made those films great is what makes \\"Prometheus\\" rate my four stars... it is visually spectacular and terrifying.<br /><br />\\"Prometheus\\" returns to the dark, Geiger-esque set design that made the original so appealing and it surprises viewers with extra-terrestrials not seen in the earlier offerings. The plot, though often predictable, revolves around seeking the origin of humans as a species and man's quest for eternal life. This \\"Alien\\" prequel takes place in the not-too-distant future, from 2089 on planet Earth until New Year's Day, 2094, on LV-223, the moon of a distant planet. The effects and cinematography are superb. And director Ridley Scott once again succeeds in making the viewer feel the fear and isolation of the hostile environment experienced by the crew of the scientific vessel. In the movie \\"Alien\\", the tag line was \\"In space, no one can hear you scream.\\" That line is still appropriate in \\"Prometheus\\".<br /><br />If I had to point out weak points of this film, it would be the dialogue and sound. I initially saw Prometheus at the theater, which is where it was intended to be viewed. Obviously you lose much in the transfer to the smaller screen. However, because of the sometimes pressured dialogue, I gained more from the movie plot-wise after watching it again on DVD (it doesn't hurt to have the closed caption feature on or the remote close by). If you can get past this, the rest should be a breeze.<br /><br />If you are an uber-critic of films you will definitely be disappointed. To the perfectionist viewer, \\"Prometheus\\" will be easy to pick apart. And no one will will be nominated for an Oscar here (althought there are good performances, especially and not surprisingly from Charlize Theron). As far as the same old, same old is concerned, there are the traditional creatures from the 1979 film, as well as a Ripley-like heroine, an android, a cavernous spacecraft, a corporate CEO heavy, and the oft-repeated stereotypical crew of both the good and the not so good. However, the movie is not silly or ridiculous and the suspense goes a long way in covering up most mistakes. The mapping \\"pups\\" are very cool, as are the new ET's. Especially impressive to me was the 5 minute or so lead-up to the opening title.<br /><br />Since I've yet to see the perfect film and in spite it's flaws, \\"Prometheus\\" has earned my praise and recommendation. It is a fun film, not a documentary. It is meant to be entertaining, not informative. So to the folks who choose to use a critical eye in determining the quality of this movie by faulting the characters for blindly putting themselves in harm's way or in the roles so often recycled in similar sci-fi thrillers, I say lighten up. It's just a movie. However, the movie is not silly or ridiculous and the suspense goes a long way in covering up most mistakes. The mapping \\"pups\\" are very cool, as are the new ET's. Especially impressive to me was the 5 minute or so lead-up to the opening title.<br /><br />Since I've yet to see the perfect film and in spite it's flaws, \\"Prometheus\\" has earned my praise and recommendation. It is a fun film, not a documentary. It is meant to be entertaining, not informative. So to the folks who choose to use a critical eye in determining the quality of this movie by faulting the characters for blindly putting themselves in harm's way or in the roles so often recycled in similar sci-fi thrillers, I say lighten up. It's just a movie. A good scarey movie.<br /><br />And without giving too much away, the end leaves plenty of room for a sequel.

B002BSHWUU|1.0|Beatles fans, throw away your garbage stereo CDs.  Instead, buy the mono box!  THIS is how you want to hear the Beatles!  Let me tell you why.<br /><br />1.  These are the mixes the boys worked on diligently with George Martin and approved.  When they were happy with the mixes, they left the studio and left George (Martin) to do the stereo mixes himself.  Believing they would have a very limited market, George did a quick and amateurish job, and it shows.  Some of the stereo mixes have goofs and quirks not heard in these mono mixes; I could point out dozens of infelicities and problems with these stereo mixes; places where the mono mixes are clearly superior.  (Those in the know will know exactly what I mean when I say \\"was in vain...\\")<br /><br />2.  The sound is actually better!  The voices are more \\"forward,\\" the drums are tighter, and the overall sound is more hard rock \\"in your face\\" (more \\"John\\") when compared with the stereo mixes, which are more distant and more mellow-sounding (more \\"Paul\\").  Even if you combine the channels on the stereo mixes to create a \\"fold down\\" mono version, it will not have the punch and presence that these mono mixes have.  In these, the sound is nicely centered with some spread, not like many of the \\"stereo\\" mixes which actually put mono sounds at the extreme edges of the sound stage.<br /><br />3.  The stereo mixes themselves are just bad.  As has been pointed out elsewhere, the first few albums were recorded on just 2 discrete tracks.  In those early days of stereo, they hadn't yet figured out the concept of just hanging two mics in front of the band and capturing a nice broad stereo soundscape.  Stereo was still a gimmick and a novelty, and the (misguided) object was to have a different, discrete sound coming from each speaker.  What we get with those stereo mixes is vocals ONLY in MONO coming from one speaker, and instrumentals in MONO from the other, with NOTHING between!  That's 2 channel sound, but it's NOT stereo.  Interesting in concept but total FAIL in execution.  Those 60's twisters might have been amused and entertained briefly by this at parties, as they stood next to one speaker with drums and guitar coming out of it and hearing the singers coming from the speaker across the room, but it is NO WAY to listen to a band!  (Just listen with headphones--you will soon rip them off and stomp on them!)<br /><br />For the next several albums, in which multi-track machines were finally being used, we still do not have a true stereo image.  Now we have the same two mono tracks at the extreme ends of the soundstage, with an additional track stuck smack in the middle.  Even in the final albums through Abbey Road, elements of the songs were still being recorded separately on separate tracks, at different times--drums on one track, vocals on another, backing vocals on a third, guitars on a fourth, other miscellaneous overdubs (piano, organ, cowbell, tambourine, whatever) on yet another track.  But they forgot one key thing:  They didn't start with a true 2-channel stereo recording of the band!  All that was done was to take these various MONO sound sources (tracks) and insert them into the stereo spectrum at different locations.<br /><br />This is difficult to describe, but listen to (for example) stereo Rubber Soul or Magical Mystery Tour with headphones.  You'll never hear a good stereo representation of the band, just a collection of several separate (and separated) mono sounds, placed at various spots across the stereo spectrum, that never manage to blend into a cohesive sound of a band.<br /><br />(Pardon me while I digress.  Keep in mind that stereo sound, for years touted as \\"3-dimensional sound!\\" is actually only creating ONE sonic dimension, specifically a straight line between the left speaker and the right speaker, or between your left ear and your right ear.  It would take at least 3 speakers, and ideally \\"quad sound,\\" that famously failed 4-speaker experiment of the 80s, to provide 2 dimensions, specifically the plane defined by those 3 or 4 speakers [and assuming you place your head in the center of that plane].  True 3-dimensional sound would require a minimum of 5 speakers; the 3 afore-mentioned planar speakers plus one above and one below the listener.  In a truly perfect world, 3-dimensional sound would be created by 8 speakers:  one in each corner of a cube-shaped room, which would allow individual sounds to be sonically placed anywhere within that room, assuming the recording was done with 8 mics, to 8 tracks.  This would be an awesome effect; much better than today's so-called \\"surround sound.\\"  You could literally sit in the middle of the band, or the Berlin Philharmonic for that matter.  When it happens, remember you heard it here first.)<br /><br />Back to the Beatles.  It would have been easy to start with a decent 2-channel stereo recording of the band with decent spread and separation, and THEN overlay all the mono overdubs (which do of course add essential details to the music) as desired.  The results would have been infinitely more satisfying than the gimmicky \\"stereo\\" of 1960s pop music we get.<br /><br />By contrast, the mono mixes are all front-and-center, with plenty of detail.  They sound like a BAND, all playing together!  The stereo mixes sound like 5 or 6 people playing in separate rooms, recorded separately, with each mono recording spliced into the stereo spectrum somewhere.<br /><br />Trust me, if you seriously love this music, which is arguably some of the finest music created in the 20th century, get it in the best sounding format, in the mixes completed and approved by the Beatles themselves!  Don't be fooled by reviewers who pop the stereo discs in their players and write 5-star reviews without truly studying and understanding the differences between the mixes.  Anyone who seriously studies this music and really LISTENS and compares will come to the same conclusions I have.  (I will point out merely to underscore my credibility:  I own and have studied all of the original US Capitol LP (vinyl, baby!) releases in both stereo and mono, the 2 Capitol CD box sets [wish they'd issue volume 3!], the stereo and mono UK LP boxes from the 1980s [beautiful sets, BTW], the singles collection and EP sets (7\\" vinyl) from the same era, all of the original UK CD reissues [there was a reason the first few CDs in this historic reissue were released in mono!], and, of course,  the new remastered stereo and mono CD box sets.)  Obsessive? Absolutely, but I hope it gives these words credence, and that you take my advice.  You won't regret it.<br /><br />Oh, I haven't even mentioned the packaging, which is of course a secondary concern, but the mono box, with each cardboard sleeve duplicating the original LP cover, is so much classier than this stereo box!

B003D585E2|5.0|1959 may have been the year that changed jazz, but this 1957 album made that year a great one, as well as becoming Art's legacy.<br /><br />Stories about the session abound and the version related by Eric C. Sedensky in his April 13, 2011 review is probably as accurate as any. There is short mention in [[ASIN:0306805588 Straight Life: The Story Of Art Pepper]] that appears to corroborate it.<br /><br />As interesting as the background is, it's the music on this album that makes it special. Part of the magic is the 'rhythm section', which was comprised of Red Garland, Paul Chambers and Philly Joe Jones - the latter two were undisputed icons whose names are revered today. I happen to love Red Garland's style although claiming him to be an icon would be inviting arguments.<br /><br />The other part of the magic of this album is Art himself. He developed his own sound and resisted changing or modifying it when Charlie Parker managed to influence not only every alto player, but every musician who heard him. It's Art's style that makes this album stand out.<br /><br />When I review an album that has sound samples on the product page I tend to avoid discussing the music and encourage potential buyers to let their ears decide whether or not the album is one they would enjoy. However, in this case I am so taken with the music that I feel compelled to comment on a few tracks. First is Jazz Me Blues, which is a 1921 composition by Tom Delaney. Bix Beiderbecke's 1924 recording of this song is probably the best rendition. Art's performance of the song on this album comes in a close second in my opinion because he is as inventive as Bix was - a mark of Art's genius.  I also loved Waltz Me Blues, which Art co-wrote with Paul Chambers. In fact, as a drummer I was so taken with Philly Joe Jones' brushwork on that track that I've spent hours studying it.<br /><br />If you've listened to the sound samples and are ready to purchase this album, hold off until you've checked out [[ASIN:B003GE69O8 Kind of Pepper]]. This ten disc set includes this album (the first disc in the set), plus nine more. Among the other nine albums are recordings chronicling Art's career from 1952 to 1959. If you purchase this set from one of the third party sellers here the cost is close to the price of this album.<br /><br />Regardless of how you purchase this album, I highly recommend it regardless of whether you are an Art Pepper fan or just love jazz from the golden era of the 1950s.003GE69O8 Kind of Pepper]]. 0449000729|5.0|As published on my blog:  victoriasreadingalcove.wordpress.com<br /><br />Some unknown years ago I managed to acquire a copy of a rather large book (1056 pages) entitled \\"Sarum.\\"  At the time I wasn't really drawn to the types of historical fiction that started with the first cooling rock.  Rutherfurd changed that opinion forever.<br /><br />The book is written about Salisbury, England and starts not quite at the first cooling rock, but at least at the point that England, destined to become an empire, becomes an island.  What I found intriguing about Rutherfurd is his ability to tell fiction through the eyes of the man and woman on the street (or around the fire).  Yes, all the events and dates we learned in world history are there, but they happen in the parlors and dining rooms, shops and farmhouses of the people of each age.  He is able to engage the reader with each turn of events by building his story using five families whose personality and physical traits seem to follow them throughout history; even as their fortunes change.<br /><br />I also found his interpretations and presentations fascinating.  One bit of story line starts with an ancient hunter/gatherer who carves a stone into a representation of his beloved wife.  This bit of carving is found during the building of the great cathedral by a worker.  Thinking that it was a precious idol from some ancient ancestor, the worker hides it high in the superstructure of the church where he is working.  A love note from the distance past preserved in a monument ostensibly constructed for love of God in the distance future.  Almost poetic, don't you think?<br /><br />Another sequence I found delightful was the great debate over whether or not women have souls as well as the spiritual struggle of many when England began the transition from Catholic to Protestant doctrine.  Rutherfurd describes the heart-rending decisions of a populace well saturated in the teaching of a Roman church taking the first steps towarda different religious practice.  Is one sure to earn eternal damnation if one accepts the Eucharist from the hand of a priest NOT ordained by Rome?  Is it sacrilege to accept the Eucharist from a man who does not believe in transubstantiation; a belief that the wine literally turns into the blood of Christ, the bread into his body?  This argument is again played out in living rooms, dining rooms, and the thoughts of the characters.<br /><br />Some would say that the book can come across as an anthology of sorts rather than a cohesive tale.  I think that Rutherfurd chose what, for him and many others, were the defining points of the place of his birth and wove them into story lines of the many generations, sometime with short vignettes, sometimes with well developed tales.  This somehow echoes the amount of information we have for each era.  He covers such things as the construction of Stonehenge, the building of the Cathedral, the arrival, departure and absorption of England's many conquerors, royal marriages, World War II, the Reformation, the Black Death and many more momentous and forgotten moments of English history.  To cover this much territory with any sense of consistency is quite a challenge.  I believe the challenge is well met.<br /><br />Meticulous in his research, skilled in his story-telling, you will find this author will walk you through the streets of Salisbury throughout its long history of else-when.  Say hello to folks when you visit.

If that sounds like a lot to cover in one book... it is, but it is nonetheless a great read for everyone.<br /><br />At the core, the premise of the book is that our obsession with standardized testing has obscured the important observation that non-cognitive skills and character traits, which we develop in the early age, can make all the difference in the long run. In fact, let's take it further: what if our schools focused more on helping children develop these traits? Why aren't they? The ultimate goal for any school should not be to teach all there is to know (that is impossible), but instead to teach you all the skills to enable you to continue learning on your own (and inspire you to do so). That's not academic aptitude, as measured by a test, that is character and a life-long life skill.

B000SEIK2S|4.0|I have to start with some background:  I have been a Heinlein fan for over thirty years, and have read every single story he published.  Although I recognize the flaws in Heinlein's works, especially the later ones, he is my favorite SF author of all time.  And the most important reason: his style of writing scientifically plausible SF in a non-technical way, focusing on characters and relationships, has never been equaled.<br /><br />I am also a big fan of Joe Haldeman's The Forever War, although I did not read it until recently.  I have no idea how I missed such a fine novel for so many years!  Thankfully that has been remedied.<br /><br />So you can imagine that when I learned that Scalzi was being touted as the \\"modern Heinlein\\", and that this book was also being compared to Haldeman's novel, I was both intrigued and initially skeptical.<br /><br />I can now predict with confidence that if you are fans of the above authors, you will likely enjoy this novel as much as I did.<br /><br />Scalzi presents technically intriguing technology, without being \\"jargon-y\\" like so much hard SF can be.  He postulates a realistic yet remarkable evolution of human society, where Earth is one isolated place and the rest of humanity seems to have \\"moved on.\\"  His characters are believable, well-rounded individuals that you can identify with.<br /><br />Scalzi also seems to have the same excellent understanding of life in the military as Heinlein - ordinary people faced with extreme situations who \\"do their best\\", some succeeding and some failing.  This is rare in SF these days; many authors seem to lack any knowledge of how military organizations work.  And, refreshingly, Scalzi does not preach political theories at his readers the way RAH often did.<br /><br />The only flaw I can point out, and the reason I give it four stars instead of five, is that the dialogue occasionally feels a bit juvenile even though the characters are most definitely mature adults.  This type of issue isnot that surprising in a debut novel; I fully expect that Scalzi's \\"voice\\" will become more refined in further works, and I look forward to finding that out shortly as I dive into the next few novels.<br /><br />Enjoy!

0062127241|2.0|In the glory days of classic rock, Pete Townshend was the rock star of choice for many an introverted, analytical fan.  Where the Stones's cool and the Beatles' regality rendered them both somewhat unrelatable to the average fan; many of us could relate to the onstage spasticity and offstage uncertainty of the Who's guitarist/songwriter.  Like us, he was looking for answers and could act unbecomingly when he couldn't find them.  It's not a great stretch to trace the beginnings of both 'seventies punk and heavy metal to Townshend's persona.  Then he kind of disappeared, surfacing only occasionally with some esoteric \\"multimedia\\" initiative or another repackaging of one of his earlier works.  Where was he?<br /><br />Apparently he was working on this book in the house which he bought, in part, for the purpose of having a place to write this book.  It was Ron Wood's house and is named The Wick.  We hear a good deal about the houses he has bought and their names, along with the names of his boats and all the famous/rich people with whom he has hung out.  Despite a good deal of self-deprecation, the overall impression that this book leaves is being present at the end of a Townshend therapy session where he exclaims:  \\"I am handsome, talented and rich and people really do like me!\\"  Instead of insight into the appeal of Meher Baba's teachings, we get another couple of pages built around his short-termed obsession with one woman or another.  Instead of hearing more about the evolution of his creative process, we learn that he's a latter day devotee to the Artist's Way handbook.  Instead of hearing about which subsequent/contemporary musicians he feels an artistic kinship, we get dollar amounts for how much he's contributed to various causes.<br /><br />Expectations were high for an autobiographical work from one of the most articulate spokespersons of the Rocker's Way.  Unfortunately, they've been drowned in a sea of Pete's self-recrimination/self-justification.  In this book, Townshend is what he always feared that he'd become:  A boring old fart.

Most recently, she has released the best-selling [[ASIN:B008FSCNTK Glad Rag Doll]].<br /><br />LIVE IN PARIS was produced by Tommy LiPuma, whose attention the singer  caught with her first, Canadian release, [[ASIN:B0000071FS Stepping Out]], and with whom she has since worked for quite some time.  The disk consists mainly of popular American standards.  It includes covers of Billy Joel's \\"Just the Way You Are\\" (a hit on U.S. smooth jazz radio); and her fellow Canadian Joni Mitchell's \\"A Case Of You.\\"  Also, Peggy Lee's \\"I Love Being Here with You.\\"  Harold Arlen's \\"Let's Fall in Love.\\"  Burt Bachrach's \\"Look of Love.\\"  Cole Porter's \\"I've Got You under My Skin.\\"  The Gershwin Brothers' \\"S' Wonderful.\\"  And jazz favorites \\"'Deed I Do,\\" \\"East of the Sun,\\" and \\"Fly Me to the Moon.\\"  The performance is also available on DVD.<br /><br />On this album, the songstress is largely backed by John Clayton on bass, with her regular accompanist Christian McBride, bass, on the twelfth track.  Jeff Hamilton is on drums, with her regular accompanist Lewis Nash on drums, on the twelfth track.  Anthony Wilson is on guitar.  The Orchestre Symphonique Europeen, conducted by Alan Broadbent, provides backing on \\"Let's Fall in Love,\\" and \\"I've Got You under My Skin.\\"<br /><br />Krall was born in Nanaimo, British Columbia, Canada, to a musical family.  The song stylist was playing piano at  four; playing jazz in a local restaurant at 15. She went to the greatly-respected Berklee College of Music in Boston on  scholarship.  She has sold more than six million albums in the US and over 15 million worldwide.  In 2009, Billboard magazine named her the second Jazz artist of the 2000-09 decade, establishing her as one of the best-selling artists of her time. She is the only jazz singer to have eight albums debuting at the top of the Billboard Jazz Albums.  To date, she has won two Grammy Awards and eight Juno Awards. She has also earned nine gold, three platinum, and seven multi-platinum albums.  Krall and British musician Elvis Costello were married in 2003 at Elton John's estate outside London. Their twin sons, Dexter Henry Lorcan and Frank Harlan James, were born in 2006 in New York City.<br /><br />The artist recalls that on her first conversation with composer/arranger Johnny Mandel, she told him that she was both a singer and a pianist. Mandel replied,\\" Oh, so you're a hyphenate! Are you a singer-pianist or a pianist-singer?\\" Krall  then confirmed that her favorite singers have all played piano too: she lists Dinah Washington, Roberta Flack, Shirley Horn, Fats Waller, Andy Bay, and \\"especially\\" Carmen McRae: \\"ultimately\\" Nat King Cole.  She considered the late songstress Rosemary Clooney to be an important mentor for her.  Krall knows how to swing a song, ability certainly in full view on this album; gives it its emotional due, and demonstrates a true feeling for jazz. She can be bluesy when called for, or painterly on a ballad, and, very importantly, she tends to know what the lyrics are about.  Krall's frequent sound engineer Al Schmitt recently told the Los Angeles Times, \\"More than most singers, she knows what's right for her, and she knows how to make it happen musically.\\" Deed she does.. So if you are a casual BOC fan and haven't heard \\"On Your Feet Or On Your Knees\\" you should totally check it out(if possible on vinyl until a remastered version is available, although if you don't have a turntable the CD will do...for now)! If you've never heard any of BOC's pre-\\"Agents Of Fortune\\" LP material and are a fan of intelligent, high-energy, drugged-out, hard-rock/post-psych, guitar rock then you have to check out \\"On Your Feet...\\". 0307454894|4.0|The modern German novelist Bernhard Schlink writes novels that make his readers feel and think to the very depths of their soul and mind. While storyline can be, at times, morally uncomfortable, the lessons he wants us to learn are nothing short of blessed and heroic. The time and setting is post-war Germany, when a nation is still dealing with the terrible guilt of the Holocaust. What we see on the surface is a sordid story of an older German woman named Hannah sexually exploiting a callow youth named Michael. If we can get past that initial shock of having to confront moral turpitude in its vilest form, we will be rewarded with an amazing accounting of why people do what they do to get by, even if it is wrong. At the heart of their illicit relationship comes a codependency that his desperate need to be loved and her need to overcome the stigma of being illiterate. While Hannah never shares her secret, Michael becomes her reader and gatekeeper to a world of emotions and ideas previously unknown t her. She eventually realizes that she cannot go on indulging in this relationship so suddenly disappears from his life. As Michael moves into manhood and law school, he suddenly meets up with Hannah again: this time as a spectator at her war crime trial as a Nazi prison guard at one of the camps. She will confess to everything the courts accuse her of only because she does not want to be cross-examined on a report that she cannot read. While she is able to gain the sympathy of the tribunal assigned to decide her fate in terms of not really knowing the full consequences of her actions, she still has to live with a guilty conscience of using a personal failing such as illiteracy to indulge wretched behaviour throughout her life. When she truly confronts her tragic past, only one choice remains for her.

This is typical of the novel's pacing.<br /> Most of the long gaps between action scenes were bridged by John's wit and DeMille's desire to share huge chunks of research on Yemen. If the novel was a meal and the action & tension were the meat and potatoes, the research was the vegetable, and John's quips the dessert, The Panther would consist of two ounces of meat, a tablespoon of mashed potatoes, 14 asparagus spears, and all the chocolate cake you can eat. In DeMille fan parlance, The Panther was to The Lions Game what The Gate House was to The Gold Coast.<br /> There were a couple of plot holes that I found troubling. In one, John asked, \\"What if it's raining?\\" after hearing the plan for a mission to Marib.  He was told, \\"It hasn't rained in Marib in 200 years.\\" Fifty pages later, his team touched down on a road in Marib and ran from the plane to a roadside ditch which was large enough to provide cover for all of them. I checked online and found that Marib gets about two inches of rain per year; not enough to merit a man-sized ditch. But, then again, Yemen is where Noah's Ark was supposed to have landed. Maybe the municipal planners didn't get the memo about \\"The Fire Next Time.\\"<br /> Despite the tone of this review, DeMille's John Corey Series will continue to be one of my favorites. I just wish he'd take a tip from Stephen King's non-fiction, \\"On Writing.\\" Early in his career, one of King's editors told him to always cut 10% from his first draft. In the case of The Panther, a 40% haircut would have turned this into an excellent read.

0156421178|5.0|Although Orwell's first-hand account of his experience in the leftist militia during the first year of the Spanish Civil War takes place 75 years ago, well before many of us were born, his account has direct application to our world today, and even here in the United States of America. This book is not just an account of the facts that happened in 1936-1937, it is an account of very real and very painful and deadly political mistrust, even in people that are supposedly one's allies. It is about the enormous difference between truth and the intentional and malicious propaganda that people, organizations and the media create to tell \\"their\\" story (instead of the truth). It is about how people choose to disrespect each other and treat each other worse than a vicious animal, not because of what one did to potentially merit such treatment but because of who they are and what group they belong to.<br /><br />And it is also a story of how Orwell dealt with such a disillusionment. Lionel Trilling states in the introduction, \\"He told the truth and he told it in an exemplary way, quietly, simply, with due warning to the reader that it was only one man's truth. He used no political jargon and he made no recriminations.\\" He had plenty of reasons to be hateful and bitter and to reflect that in his writing, but he chose not to. That is what makes this book so unique and especially today. We live in a world where we are overloaded with data and information. Watching and listening to all of the advertisements of both candidates for President that have been bombarding the airwaves, especially in \\"swing\\" states like Virginia shows me how unique Orwell was in his writing. Our world is full of political jargon and recriminations. The truth? Often hidden. Often intentionally. Quite the opposite of Orwell's approach.<br /><br />The horrors and atrocities that happened in that Civil War are happening today in the world. Look at Syria, for example. Situations like those described in his book and like are happening elsewhere in the world often start with the loss of civil liberties. Some say that we are starting to see some of our civil liberties be eroded in this country. Read this book and see what happens when those civil liberties are attacked or taken. It's not just the fighting and shooting at each other. It is how we start to treat each other. See it in this book and think about today. And then think about how we would act in such situations. Would we act and move forward objectively without hatred and without recriminations as Orwell did? The fact that the book can lead you to think about questions like that is what makes Orwell's writing unique and very timely, even in 2012.

0486414124|3.0|It's not surprising that \\"Northanger Abbey\\" is Jane Austen's first novel. It's not quite pulled together as smoothly as her more famous and well-regarded works, and the dialogue is stilted at times.  However, the novel is still enjoyable enough that it's worth investing the time to read its mere 200 pages.<br /><br />Beginning novelists are told to \\"write what you know,\\" and a young Jane Austen followed that advice.  \\"Northanger Abbey\\" tells the tale of a 17-year-old girl (Catherine) of a respectable family that lives in the countryside. Catherine is given her first real opportunity to see life beyond her rural village when she's asked to accompany an older couple on a six-week trip to Bath.  Once there, Catherine is introduced to \\"society,\\" and her naive, straightforward way of looking at the actions and words of society people provides for satire and criticism of the pretensions of upper-crust life at the time.<br /><br />Many things are skewered, such as the idleness of time spent at bath, the lemming-like surges of people to the same places at the same time, and the rigid rules for manners and conduct that must be learned.  But perhaps the thing most satirized is women.  For example, Catherine's benefactor, Mrs. Allen, spends all of her time shopping for clothes and marking every occasion by what she and others are wearing.  Also, Catherine's first Bath acquaintance, Isabella, constantly says one thing when she means the exact opposite and is always on the lookout for a new angle. (Remarkable how those traits continue today to be the primary cliches about how women spend their free time.)<br /><br />Meanwhile, Catherine stands in opposition to those two foolish women.  Though not a beauty, she attracts the attention of two men.  One is Isabella's brother John, who is a ridiculously boastful ass.  Catherine quickly sees through his bluster.  The other, Mr. Tilney, is a charmer who turns out to be a genuine gentleman.  Things ultimately work out for Catherine andMr. Tilney to live happily ever after, despite the machinations of John and some misunderstandings that involve Isabella, as well as Catherine's brother, and Tilney's sister Eleanor.<br /><br />Other reviewers have said that the book satirizes the gothic romances that were popular at the time, and I guess that critique is true.  Austen goes to great pains to humorously distinguish the plot of her book from the intensity of those novels, and she makes it clear that her book is rooted in reality, not the supernatural realm that is the domain of the gothic.<br /><br />However, I detected a great deal of respect for those types of books.  The narrator does attack gothic novels, and Austen also puts criticisms into the mouths of some of the characters.  But she allows her heroine Catherine to defend those books because they: 1) Are enjoyable; and 2) Provide insights into human nature that are not readily available in non-fiction books.  Given that the heroine Catherine is a devotee of gothic novels and that she triumphs in the end, in part because she uses the wisdom of those novels to understand people's motivations, I think that Austen is gentler towards popular fiction than many reviewers suggest.  Isabella and Mr. Tilney, the other two favored characters, also declare their enjoyment of popular novels.  If anything, I think Austen is defending the novels as providing some understanding about human nature, even while mostly serving as diversions for women wealthy enough to have leisure to read.

B009VA1FN6|5.0|The Secret Keeper is the fourth novel from popular Australian author Kate Morton, whose previous books such as the The House At Riverton and The Forgotten Garden, have enjoyed international success.<br /><br />In the Secret Keeper, Morton grabs the reader's attention with the first chapter as sixteen year old Laurel witnesses a tragic altercation between her mother and a stranger. Nearly fifty years later Laurel's latent curiosity prompts her to investigate Dorothy's past, inspired by an inscription in a copy of a Peter Pan, a photo of Dolly linking arms with a friend, Vivian, and the vague whispers of her dying mother, slowly piecing together an extraordinary story.<br /><br />As the narrative shifts between Laurel's search into her mother's past in present-day England to London during the Blitz, the reader is witness to Dorothy's life. A headstrong and vivacious teenager, Dolly flees her staid family to make a life for herself in London, certain she is destined to become something special. She imagines having a life of luxury, social standing and wealth, like that enjoyed by Vivian Jenkins, which seems possible when she becomes the companion of the rich, eccentric and elderly, Lady Gwendolyn but when Dolly's dreams sour, she is devastated. Despite the adoration of her boyfriend, Jimmy, Dolly concocts a plan to claim what she believes is her destiny, triggering a cascade of events that lead to tragedy.<br /><br />In a vividly drawn setting, Morton creates a cast of intriguing, believable characters who are motivated by wistful dreams and dark secrets. As their relationships unraveled and the plot grew more intricate I was drawn into the twists and turns of the story, that leads to a stunning conclusion that will take most readers by surprise.<br /><br />Finely crafted, The Secret Keeper is both an engrossing mystery and a sweeping historical saga. A compelling tale of love, loss and betrayal this is a wonderful read from a gifted storyteller.

B005LAIIE4|5.0|The Short: Wreck-It Ralph is a classic. From the slick animation, the great sense of humor, nostalgia inducing references and cameos, and the surprisingly adept and emotional story, Disney's Wreck-it Ralph is the best animated comedy since Tangled, and one of Disney's best animated films ever crafted.<br /><br />Street Fighter, Pac-Man, Q-bert; widely known and considered classic games. But a \\"new challenger has entered the ring\\" in the form of old school, Donkey Kong inspired retro arcade game, Wreck-it Ralph. Follow the misadventures of Wreck-it Ralph, voiced by John C. Reilly, as he attempts to become a hero by jumping though various video games. I don't want to spoil any of the plot, but it is incredibly well told and is quite surprising in the end. It has that classic Disney emotion, but with a most unique \\"video game-y\\" twist. In the end, Wreck-it Ralph teaches some great lessons, but it is also neither mundane nor juvenile, and that's why it's a winner.<br /><br />The cast here couldn't fit the characters better. John C. Reilly as the big guy Wreck-it Ralph, Sarah Silverman as the spirited and surprisingly funny Vanellope von Schweetz, Jane Lynch as the stoic and hilarious Sergeant Calhoun, and Jack McBrayer as the lovable and yet again laugh- out-loud Fix-it Felix Junior. The movie is absolutely hilarious; the performances from all of the actors fit their roles perfectly and couldn't be funnier. They couldn't have picked a better voice cast, honestly to goodness.<br /><br />The animation continues the high pedigree that Disney has become famous for. Its bright and lively action is wonderful to watch, and combined with great facial animations make for a great and emotional experience. But the winner here is the way that they have adapted the old- school style of video game animation into the film itself. You'll know what I mean when you see the movie. It makes for a truly unique, one of a kind experience! Sony's 4K presentation is crisp and vibrant.<br /><br />The thing to understand though is that with its focus on video game cameos and references, don't worry! You don't have to have any knowledge of video games to understand or enjoy Wreck-it Ralph. The story and main characters are all part of the film's story and world. Rather than using the references as a crutch, they're used more as a springboard into new and unexplored fictional worlds.<br /><br />Granted, gamers of all ages are going to love the care and attention taken when putting in the huge amount of references, cameos, and little bits of easter eggs spritzed and scattered throughout Wreck-it Ralph, making for a truly nostalgic inducing experience.<br /><br />And those classic Disney trademarks, from great characters to a well told story, are all here and are much more than side attractions. The twist is great, the concepts are fresh, and the level of imagination at work revives my faith in the animated genre. There's still plenty left in this old dog after all.<br /><br />And so I have to end this review by asking, \\"Are you tired of the same old washed up animated feature film? Feel like you're just too old for childish animated movies?\\" Wreck-it Ralph is the perfect cure. And it's meant for that group of movie goers looking for something more than just another animated money pit. It's laugh out loud funny, exciting and fresh, incredibly inventive and gleefully unique at every turn.<br /><br />It's a classic no doubt, and Wreck-it Ralph will be one of those movies on my \\"favorites\\" shelf for decades to come. B005QJZ5FA|5.0|I wanted to start off saying that, as a whole, Born To Die is an album that definitely requires listening to get used to. Rather than being outwardly catchy, the songs slowly begin to imbue themselves into your mind. A standard pop song is like disappearing ink; it stains itself in your mind, darkly and quickly, and stays strong for a little bit, and then disappears from your memory completely. The songs in Born To Die are more like a stain that spreads across fabric. It doesn't make a big impact initially, but eventually creeps into a big permanent mark that sticks. Lana Del Rey's voice strikes me as tender, emotional, and real. If you hear artists (or do they even deserve that title?) like Katy Perry, Rihanna, and Britney Spears, their voices sound so aseptically clean and boring from the ravages of autotune. There are imperfections and differing inflections to Lana Del Rey's voice that personalize the music and make it feel like in each song she is revealing some kind of personal secret. Even though I did give Ms. Del Rey five stars, I would truly give Born to Die a score of 9 out of 10. The docked point isn't for any particular reason, but in comparison to albums like Madonna's Ray of Light, Joni Mitchell's Blue, and Carly Simon's Spy, it just doesn't measure up quite as well. But nonetheless, it is a new favorite album, and lyrically, it measures up as an equal to the albums I've listed. In all fairness, for an album, that takes some time to fully understand, I certainlly think this is a 2010's masterpiece.

Highly re-watchable considering some of the most shocking and at times potentially repellant scenes to ever appear in a mainstream film. It still is director Danny Boyle's best film to date.<br /><br />Regarding Lionsgate's blu-ray of Trainspotting, there has been a bit of controversy. There had been a few years back a 2 disc collector's edition of the film which presented it in its international cut that differed very slightly from the American R rated cut. To avoid an NC-17 rating, a couple of seconds were trimmed from the sex scene involving Ewan McGregor's character and a girl he meets at a club. The filmmakers also had to substitute a few shots amounting to only about 3 or so seconds in this same sex scene and also substitute a later shot of a needle breaking Ewan's arm during his overdose scene with a shot of his face instead. To be honest, the slight changes in the American R rated cut are imperceptible unless you've seen the uncut version and even then, it's really not a big deal at all.<br /><br />For the film's American blu-ray release though, Lionsgate used the R rated version instead of the uncut international version. While I was ever so slightly disappointed in that fact, the positives of this hi-def release greatly outweigh this particular fact. Colors are greatly improved along with much better contrast and detail compared to the DVD. In fact, the blu-ray makes the DVD look positively washed out in comparison. There is a nice filmic layer of grain throughout and I couldn't spot any instances of any digital noise reduction. This blu-ray simply blows the older DVD out of the water and is truly like seeing the film all over again for the first time. Audio is presented in lossles 5.1 DTS sound.<br /><br />All of the extras from the 2 disc DVD collector's edition were carried over. If you own the prior DVD and are a completist like myself, I just threw away the pointless digital copy and instead kept the first disc of the 2-disc DVD to still have the uncut intertional version. There is a 2 disc blu-ray release in Europe that contains the uncut version but it is region B locked so unless you have a region free blu-ray player, the Lionsgate blu-ray is the best way to go.<br /><br />While I'm not sure why Lionsgate put the R rated cut on the blu-ray, that is the only thing that slightly keeps this release from being definitive. But it really is a very minor differance. Like I mentioned earlier though, the picture quality is a quantum leap over the DVD and is still well worth the upgrade. Penguin is the parent publisher of this book and the company ran afoul early-on with the federal government (US) over its pricing practices. I recently learned that Penguin terminated its relationship with Overdrive, which almost all public libraries use to make e-books (including Kindle) available to library patrons. This means that \\"Winter of the World\\" and all other Penguin titles are not available to those of us that use public libraries.<br /><br />As for the book itself, $20 is an awful lot of money to pay out in return for the reading experience. I am 62 years old, too young to have served in World War II, but plenty young enough to know WWII veterans. When I was old enough to take an interest, these vets were either in their late 30s or mid 40s. Of all the human conflicts that I have read about and/or talked to participants about, World War II is one of the very few conflicts in world history where mankind had a clear choice to make: good vs. evil.<br /><br />For the most part, World War II serves as a patchy tapestry for the characters in \\"Winter of the World.\\" So much was glossed over. While the Jewish Holocaust is mentioned in the book, the concentration camps get no play at all. The Battle of Britain (known as \\"The Blitz\\") in the book has gone down in history as \\"Britain's Finest Hour.\\" Yet, except for a brief plot line where Daisy drives an ambulance in the Blitz, very little is said about it.<br /><br />One of the most incongruent and contrived scenes in the book takes place in Pearl Harbor. Senator Gus Dewar and his family are invited to breakfast aboardthe \\"USS Arizona.\\" So they are traveling across the harbor to battleship row and the \\"Arizona\\" when, you guessed it, the Japanese Zeroes arrive. An errant bullet from a Zero kills Woody's fianc. This twist in the plotline was improbable and incongruent addition. First, to get to Hawaii, the family had to fly there. In 1941, flights from the US mainland to Hawaii were extremely rare. Then, they just happen to be on the launch when the Japanese strike. The death of Woody's fianc makes no sense in the context of the book. We leave Woody as he is cradling his fianc, and he doesn't show up again in the book until at least a hundred pages later. His fianc gets one more passing mention, but Woody, by the time we hear from him again is on to \\"bigger and better things,\\" as they say.<br /><br />The first book, \\"Fall of Giants,\\" had interesting characters and the tapestry of World War I shines. Follett does a good job explaining the world's obsession with \\"class,\\" especially that of Britain, Russia, and to a lesser extent, Germany. The characters are well fleshed out. Follett's narrative into the causes of World War I make for an absorbing history lesson. For the most part, the author basically throws the characters from the first book into the dustbin for \\"Winter of the World.\\" He uses the offspring from the characters in \\"Fall of Giants\\" to take up the load in the sequel. I felt \\"robbed\\" in that his \\"old\\" characters got so little play. For example, Billy and Fitz were in their prime of life when the second book started. They were just old enough to be able to assume the mantle of responsibility and political strength, but they weren't around.<br /><br />The only thing that I can say as I conclude this is that I hope the third book is better and that I hope the pricing is a lot fairer.

1572815108|5.0|As a tarot collector, the Thoth Tarot has been one that always intrigued me.  Designed by Aleister Crowley and Painted by Lady Frieda Harris, this one is probably the third most popular deck after the Rider-Waite-Smith Tarot and Tarot of Marseilles.  With an intriguing collage of symbols, this is a deck that caters to the occult like no other.<br /><br />The Thoth Tarot from US Games comes in two sizes:<br />- 4.375\\" x 2.75\\" deck which is 0.375\\" smaller than standard US Games decks.<br />- 5.5\\" x 3.75\\" deck which is ~1\\" bigger and wider than standard US Games decks.<br /><br />The smaller deck is easier to handle and includes two additional versions of the Magus, while the images are easier to see on the larger one.  However, the larger deck lacks the additional cards.<br /><br />The back of these cards is non-reversible, showing a Rosicrucian cross, colored yellow up, white and black down, red left and blue right on top of a green spark, on a crisscrossing diamond pattern containing small symbols of wands, cups, swords, and disks.<br /><br />The Major Arcana are numbered at the top, in roman numerals starting at 0 with The Fool.  Comparing these to the RWS Tarot, I noticed that the following:<br /><br />I. The Magician - I. The Magus<br />VIII. Strength - XI. Lust<br />X. The Wheel of Fortune - X. Fortune<br />XI. Justice - VIII. Adjustment<br />XIV. Temperance - XIV. Art<br />XX. Judgement - XX. The Aeon<br />XXI. The World - XXI. The Universe<br /><br />These cards are labeled at the bottom, with an Hebrew character and an elemental, planetary, or astrological symbol included with the label.<br /><br />The Minor Arcana are arranged in four suits: wands, cups, swords and discs.  These corresponds to the elements of Fire, Water, Air, and Earth.<br /><br />The pips are numbered at the top.  The Aces of each suit are labeled as such at the bottom while pips 2 to 10 are labeled with a key word.  These cards are illustrated, but focus only on the symbols of each suit, and are devoid of any figure, human or otherwise.  These include small symbols corresponding to the planet and astrological sing associated with them.<br /><br />The court cards are only labeled at the bottom as Princess, Prince, Queen and Knight of each suit.  These are associated to elements of Earth, Air, Water, and Fire, correspondingly.<br /><br />The deck comes in a fitting box with a little white book (LWB).  In the LWB, The cards a numbered starting on 1 (The Fool) and concluding with 78.  The Ace of Wands is numbered 23, The Ace of Cups is numbered 37, The Ace of Swords is numbered 51, and The Ace of Discs is numbered 65.<br /><br />A lot of books have been written exploring the richness of symbols in this deck, so I'm not going to pretend to scratch the surface in this review. B008JAFXOQ|5.0|{4.5 Stars}<br /><br />\\"Margaret\\" plays like a good modern novel. The acting, script, and cinematography are incredibly realistic, and the story is intelligently presented without being overly artsy or high-brow.<br /><br />My take on it: After witnessing and being an unwitting participant in a tragic bus accident, bright, promising, but very frenetic NYC high school senior Lisa Cohen finds it harder than ever to find connection with anyone around her. Ironically, this prevents her from understanding why everyone around her has the same problem. As she says herself during one of the numerous altercations with her rising Broadway actress mother, \\"People don't relate to each other. . . They're totally disconnected.\\"<br /><br />On this subject, there are a lot of people screaming at each other here, and they usually don't even recall how the screaming began. They always stop screaming before it gets really tiresome, but the fights are crucial to the theme of people just acting out with no attempt to understand or empathize. The very fine acting and dialogue prevent \\"Margaret\\" from descending into what it could have been: A hackneyed soap opera/New York melodrama of the sort we've seen plenty of times before.<br /><br />I found Lisa harder and harder to take as the film progressed. Sometimes it seemed that she should be a little less of a selfish \\"drama queen,\\" but, again, this negative development may be deliberate on the part of the creators and helps pose the question of who's really crazy and who's really sane.<br /><br />There is a slow, steady tension to this film, plenty of interesting stuff happens, and there are all kinds of meaningful subplots. It often seems to meander, but everything's relevant in the end. Yet, \\"Margaret\\" is driven more by its various themes than it is by plot or character. I like it because it's so different from most current films; in fact, it's the first recent film I've seen that I'll probably want to see again. Nevertheless, people who just want to be entertained without having to sit back and analyze what they're watching will probably not want to sit through 2.5 hours of this.just want to be entertained without having to sit back and analyze what they're watching will probably not want to sit through 2.5 hours of this.

B000QCS8TW|4.0|It's been ages since I originally purchased this book on my Kindle. I saw the size of the book and when I got my Kindle it was one of the first purchases I made. I figured it would be better to carry it on that slim device than to lug around the rather large book. I wanted to read the book prior to the premier of the show but... well that didn't happen. So my goal shifted; I wanted to read the first book before the second season began and that also didn't happen. Well, I gave it a try at least. I began reading this book in April just after I moved to Virginia and didn't have a job. I would spend my mornings putting out job applications and then by late afternoon I'd sit back and read a little. But the size of this book overwhelmed me, not that I haven't read anything of this size before, but for some reason the slow moving percentage on my Kindle wasn't being very helpful. Then I got my temp job and this book was put down.<br /><br />Back and forth over the past five months I went. I would read a new book, put it down, then read 50 pages of Game of Thrones. Not only that but with trying to maintain a regularly updated book blog with ramblings about books I've read it's hard to just guarantee a number of days to read this huge book. However, I finished a book and went back to GoT for my few chapter read through and realized I was actually pretty darn close to being finished. Only, like, 200 pages left! So I read it in a flash and loved every moment of it then sat back and wondered why I hadn't just read it in one go to begin with.<br /><br />Nonetheless, let's talk about the book for the very few people out there who haven't read it. Because, it seems, I am the last person in the world who got around to starting this series. If you've seen the show it's a lot like the book; they did a very good job at portraying the characters and many of the scenes in my opinion. Still, this book is long so obviously it has much more detail and scenery than the show does. If you've seen the show but have not read the book I'd suggest doing so!<br /><br />While I wasn't keen on carrying around a copy of the book because it was so large I do wish, in a way, that I had that opportunity so that I could flip back and forth between the maps and family trees. It would have helped as the cast of the book is huge and the families are very wide spread and detailed. I have forever had issues of remembering people's names, book characters included, and had it not been for the fact that I had already watched the tv show and had faces to place with the names I probably would have been more lost as to who was who and how they were connected.<br /><br />The story is good, the imagery is good, the description is good. This book is good. If you have a fascination with anything remotely like Tudor history, Arthurian legend or the long, detailed writing in Lord of the Rings then A Song of Ice and Fire is perfect for you. Dragons, princesses, secrets and swords fill its pages and often times left my head spinning. This book has a touch of fantasy but it doesn't go overboard. You aren't stuck feeling like you just slipped into the land of the Sugar Plum Fairy or Hogwarts. It's slipped in so casually that you find yourself, whilst reading the book, to just accept what they are speaking of and not think twice about if dragons exist or the dead can rise and kill.<br /><br />Martin may put a little too much emphasis into certain details but I suspect they all come around to meaning something and he certainly helps you to picture the world he has created. It reads like some fantastic part of history yet the characters are certainly living and breathing at your ear, over your shoulder, while you go from page to page. Often times I'll read books by authors who have long since left this earth and I'm left feeling melancholy. \\"Why don't people write like this anymore? Why don't they put detail into their books and write so beautifully?\\" and I think I've discovered that there are authors who write in such ways and Martin is one of them. It's refreshing to be able to read a book so beautifully written and with such perfect detail that is current and published within my lifetime. Could it have been shortened down at some points? Certainly. Every other chapter I found at least a few pages that I could have gone without but what are you going to do? It's not like I didn't already know this was going to be a long book when I began it.<br /><br />It does have its fair share of sex scenes, incest, and rape so be forewarned of that those of you who like to avoid such plot. But it's relevant to the story, or so it seems... most of the time, so it's kind of worth talking about. Martin leaves a lot of tidbits of information through out the book which you can pick apart in your own time and wonder what it all could mean. Apparently, it's a Thing fans of the series like to do and I can understand why they would when it spans such long periods of time between publications of books. In that regard, I'm glad I waited to pick up the books so that I won't have to wait forever for each book to come out. Granted, when A Song of Ice and Fire was first published I was ten and this was way beyond my reading comprehension but at least now I can take my time, play catch up, and maybe once I'm completely caught up with the books I can join the countless others who eagerly await the next book in the series.<br /><br />I think what I liked best about the books was that the characters grow and change while you read. Often times you are able to witness how the surrounding events will alter a person or you are simply given privy to details otherwise unnoticed. I started the book with a dead set group of characters whom I liked and ones I disliked but by the end of the book that list had shuffled a little bit. Some of the characters I disliked at first (Sansa, for example) I had begun to like a little more by the end. While I have many other books I have to get through before I start A Clash of Kings I will be happy when I have that opportunity and look forward to it. There are many people out there who love this book and consider it a work of art, the best thing they had ever read, and swear by it. There are others who refuse to speak nothing but negative things about the book - it just did not work for them. For me, I liked it, I enjoyed it, and while I may not be standing on my office's roof proclaiming to the people waiting for their lunches that they must read this book - I still will quietly refer friends to it who are looking for a good tale.e are authors who write in such ways and Martin is one of them. 159420411X|5.0|I've enjoyed reading Nate Silver's 538 blog since I learned of it during the 2008 election season.  He was a breath of fresh air then, and remains so today.  In my profession, I involve myself with creating, analyzing, and teaching about mainly deterministic predictive models of fluids, using models similar in spirit to those Silver describes which have had success in giving us better predictions of the weather.  Silver does an outstanding job conveying to a lay audience their strengths and weaknesses.  Not every detail is perfect; Lorenz's seminal work \\"Deterministic Nonperiodic Flow\\"  appeared in 1963; Silver only recognizes some later work.  Nevertheless, Silver is properly appreciative and skeptical of determinism, a quality which is missing from the writings of some celebrators of \\"Big Data.\\"  He did himself and his readers a service in consulting with MIT's Kerry Emanuel, one of the more temperate experts on greenhouse effect modeling whose serious scientific writings have persuaded me of many things.<br /><br />Silver also effectively captures some of my concerns regarding predictions that have weaker foundation in a priori models but are nevertheless of great potential utility to humankind.  He has a nice discussion of the role of statistics and Bayesian inference that properly should be associated with such predictions, and does the world a service in asking us to consider the track record of public prognosticators as we decide how much credence to lend to their thoughts.<br /><br />He is to be commended for taking on a broad variety of subjects in today's world where prediction is used.  Any general reader should not be put off by the quibbling expert in such fields, as no doubt Silver has missed a nuance or two.  Most readers will be rewarded by gaining, as did I, a better appreciation of how prediction is critical to our modern world, and how to ask skeptical questions of modern-day snake-oil salespeople.

0385535147|2.0|I am a man of eternal hope.  Many years ago, I started reading Grisham with \\"The Pelican Brief\\" and \\"The Firm\\" and thought \\"Hey, this guy is COOL!\\"  Then came the dark years of one boiler plate effort after another until I finally gave up.  Until the recent rave reviews for \\"The Racketeer.\\"<br /><br />Alas, naif that I am, I was again taken in by another excellent example of marketing hype.<br /><br />The basic premise of the story is simple:  Malcolm Bannister, a simple, small time lawyer is wrongly jailed as part of a federal investigation of financial fraud.  In the real world, a federal judge and his mistress are brutally murdered, leaving the FBI and Justice Department chasing their tails in a mad tizzy and getting nowhere.  In desperation, they offer a $150,000 reward for information on the killer(s).  Enter our hero who promises them the name and motive of the killer in return for a full pardon, entry into the witness protection program and, of course, the $150,000.  Some gnashing of teeth by the arrogant feds but they finally (of course) agree and Bannister is released.<br /><br />Up to this point a very good story, tightly written, with excellent character development and a \\"what the heck is going on?\\" plot.  But then all falls apart.  For the next 100 pages, our hero becomes involved in murkier and murkier schemes, constantly twisting our belief and the rules of basic logic.  Need to get from point A to point B?  Hire a private jet.  Need to start a fake business?  Hire a corporate lawyer.  How about an unscrupulous dealer in precious metals?  Look in the yellow pages.  And while all of this is going on, keep telling the reader over and over, \\"damn, when I planned this two years ago, I NEVER thought it would really work!\\"<br /><br />The author used an irritating style of switching from Bannister speaking in first person to relating the activities of various federal agents and, of course, drop dead accomplices, in third person.  The basic premise is apparently to build this beautifully complicated story with all of the parts carefully interlinked.  What he winds up with a large tangled mess of twine.<br /><br />Indeed, the ball becomes so complicated that the last chapter is essentially the English drawing room scene from countless Sherlock Holmes and Miss Marple mysteries.  In this case, Grisham actually has Bannister tell the reader \\"OK, this is what you thought was happening, but this what we really were doing.\\"  By this time you are so disgusted with the entire mess you couldn't care less who is really the villian, who is really my long lost buddy or whether the entire Federal government can really be that stupid.<br /><br />All in all, a useless waste of time.

B00280LYIC|5.0|Rick Riordan has hit on a winning formula in the Percy Jackson series! Lots of adventure aimed directly at the 10-13 year old reluctant reader. The story line and characters are as addictive as Rowling's Harry Potter books, but instead of using wizardry and witchcraft, Riordan empowers his heroes and heroines through the magic of Greek mythology. Tons of monster-fighting, problem-solving, and even a bit of age-appropriate romance thrown in as the characters age along with the target audience. As a reader, a parent, and a middle-school English teacher, I cannot say enough good about Percy Jackson and the Lightning Thief! At least a dozen parents have thanked me for introducing this story to their sons, who would not read a book until this one came along, and who have now read and re-read the entire series. I even know of some teenagers (both boys and girls) who had a race to see who could finish the latest book first! Not only are they entertained by these stories, but they are also learning about the root mythology of Western civilization while traveling to all the major landmarks of the U.S.A. (and, in the Heroes of Olympus series, across the Atlantic to Europe as well); when they get on to high school and have to study Homer's Odyssey and Iliad, they are making straight A's without effort! Last year I read the series aloud to my son, who has always been a struggling reader, and now he is re-reading it independently and loving it even more the second time around. DO NOT BE TURNED AWAY BY THE POOR MOVIE ADAPTATION!

B003Y5H4YI|3.0|The Debt is a spy-thriller that focuses more on character development than action.  The time is 1965.  Three Israeli Mossad agents are tasked with capturing the Nazi war criminal Dieter Vogel, also known as \\"the Surgeon of Birkenau,\\" and bringing him from East Berlin to Israel to stand trial for atrocities committed against the Jewish people.  Things do not go as planned, however, and the agents must improvise.  The movie alternates between the mission in 1965 and the aftermath in 1997, when the three are now old and famous, but bear a terrible secret.  Will they tell the truth or continue to perpetuate a lie?<br /><br />The acting is strong (particularly Helen Mirren as old Rachel and Jessica Chastain as young Rachel), and the directing is tight, maintaining suspense till the end.  The blu-ray transfer is great--both audio and visuals are what one would expect from a recent release.  The bonus features include the typical director's commentary and making-of documentaries.<br /><br />Parental advisory: The Debt contains some language and violence, including discussions of Holocaust atrocities.  While there is no nudity, there is implied sex and three uncomfortable-to-watch gynecological examinations with reproduction-related dialogue.  This is not a movie for pre-teens.<br /><br />I recommend The Debt.  It does not have the flash of a Jason Bourne movie, but is more realistic.  The agents, while skilled and physically fit, are nevertheless flesh and blood people with emotions.  It is worth seeing.

It's also heavy on the unstated but implicit condemnation of those responsible for the loss of our great national industrial spinal column and the erosion of the \\"social contract\\" of the 1940's, a covenant that built America's middle class. The name of the album is clearly metaphorical...America's great economic beating heart has mutated into a \\"wrecking ball\\" and Bruce wants to sing about it.<br />In short, Bruce is older but all there. Solid. Unwavering. Vintage Bruce Springsteen...working class hero, rock-auteur. I love it.

B008AS5UAO|2.0|I fell for the hype.<br /><br />When Deutsche Grammophon announced this release in Summer 2012, I looked forward to a sleek, slick, modern performance with outstanding singing, playing, and conducting. Perhaps, too, I was swayed by the presence on the podium of Yannick N&eacute;zet-S&eacute;guin, the young, exciting, incoming music director of my local band, the Philadelphia Orchestra.<br /><br />I could not have been more disappointed.<br /><br />The problems begin from the start. The first bars make it clear that this performance will be informed by the sound-worlds of the historically-informed performance (HIP) movement: a less weighty orchestral sound, restrained use of vibrato, and so on. Nor is this in itself a problem. Yet, once the conductor, ensemble, and producers have set this tone, I had imagined that they would stick with it.<br /><br />And it's when we hear the voices that the problems become evident: they are too big for this conception. Ildebrando D'Arcangelo may be one of the great Don Giovannis of this generation, but on this recording, he overpowers his Leporello, Luca Pisaroni. I hear a Don Giovanni who is mean, cynical, and brutal, to whom a buffo counterweighto seems ineffective and, at the end of the day, not even very funny. Similarly, Joyce DiDonato's Donna Elvira is marred by her vibrato, which I find almost unlistenable, but which, at a minimum, obscures those hints of gullibility and naivet&eacute; that, early on in the opera, seems to be an integral aspect of her character.<br /><br />Still, the most serious problems are on the podium. N&eacute;zet-S&eacute;guin's conducting, rather than in assisting to move the drama forward, frequently bogs it down. I had the sense that his approach was not well thought out and that he needed to live with the piece for much longer before committing it to record. Time will almost certainly give him the opportunity to refine his conception, to synthesize the practices of HIP with the capabilities of voices suited to a big house like the Met.<br /><br />In the meantime, I recommend that listeners look to the recordings by Ren&eacute; Jacobs and Nikolaus Harnoncourt to hear two of the best representations of this work as heard through two of the leading of the practitioners of HIP, the former on eighteenth-century instruments, the latter with the (modern) Royal Concertgebouw Orchestra. And listeners interested in an older tradition can always turn to recordings by Busch, Furtw&auml;ngler, Friscay, and Giulini.

1401207529|5.0|Somewhere along the east coast of the United States, lies a major metropolitan area known as Gotham City. From the outside, it looks like a peaceful and prosperous city, but below the surface, it is a crime-ridden hell-hold of greed, corruption, graft, sin, and villainy. Viscous crime lords like Carmine &#34;The Roman&#34; Falcone, and Sal &#34;The Boss&#34; Maroni have an iron grip on the city's economy and politics. Even Gotham's finest are no strangers to corruption. Cops like Detective Flass and Commissioner Loeb are being paid off by the mob, and in return give them protection. It's almost as if there is no hope for Gotham City. No hope except for.... THE BATMAN!!!<br /><br />BATMAN: YEAR ONE is the ultimate retelling of Batman's origin! It defines who Batman is, how he came to be, and what he fights against like never before! Frank Miller (author of THE DARK KNIGHT RETURNS, SIN CITY, and 300) builds up on the original two-page origin story created by Bob Kane and Bill Finger in 1939, and redefines it for a modern generation! We get to see how corrupted Gotham is from the view points of both Jim Gordon and Batman. Jim Gordon is a young police officer that has just moved to Gotham City from Chicago, with his pregnant wife Barbra. After joining the GCPD, Gordon is assigned as a lieutenant to Detective Flass' unit. Immediately Gordon sees how low the police department has fallen. He witnesses Flass taking bribes from drug dealers and learns that Commissioner Loeb is a personal friend of crime lords like &#34;The Roman.&#34; The stress of cleaning up the police department, along with trying to support and protect his pregnant wife from harm, leads Lt. Gordon to carrying the burden of a dark secret from everyone else.<br /><br />In Batman's point of view, his alter-ego Bruce Wayne has returned to Gotham City after a 12 year long absence. He is now fully trained, and ready to take on the scum of Gotham. However, he still lacks one crucial element: the power to install fear in his enemies. He realizes this on his first night of crime fighting, when he is brutally beaten by a gang of prostitutes, and shot by the police. He is able to escape back to Wayne Manor before he succumbs to his injuries. As he is trying to figure out how to scare his enemies, a bat comes crashing through his window. Knowing that bats frightened him when he was a boy, he decides to take up the mantle of a bat to turn his fear as a weapon against his enemies. It was only after that night, that he truly became the Batman. The dark and menacing figure of the night, who uses fear against those who prey on the fearful.<br /><br />Frank Miller uses both viewpoints to create the sensational story of Batman's first year of crime fighting. He tells us not just of how Bruce Wayne became Batman, but also of how he introduced into the setting of Gotham. He is not the legendary crime fighter that he is today. He is still inexperienced, vulnerable to injury, distrusted by the police, and is continuously building his way up from a novice crime fighter, to the dark knight. Miller also expands Jim Gordon's role in the Batman universe. In earlier comics he was thought of as an ordinary and elderly police commissioner who simply was allies with Batman, because he helped bring in criminals. But Frank Miller gives us a completely different outtake on Gordon. That he is an average man who has devoted himself to cleaning up the corruption in not only Gotham City, but in the police department as well. He does not fully support Batman's methods, but allows him to carry on his vigilante activities because of the good he does for Gotham. Frank Miller created the Commissioner Gordon that we know today.<br /><br />It is a truly remarkable story that only the genius behind THE DARK KNIGHT RETURNS, could've created. Miller breaks the chains of Batman's original origin story, and gives us a realistic story of two men's crusade on saving their city from corruption. A story that would change Batman's world forever, and inspire the film BATMAN BEGINS. You can never call yourself a Batman fan without reading the legendary BATMAN: YEAR ONE!he film BATMAN BEGINS.
